<p><b>Cuba</b>, officially the <b>Republic of Cuba</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:RCUB.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/28/Rep%C3%BAblica_de_Cuba.ogg" class="internal" title="República de Cuba.ogg"><span class="unicode" lang="es"><i>República de Cuba</i></span></a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:RCUB.ogg" class="mw-redirect" title="File:RCUB.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>), is a country comprising the island of Cuba as well as <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a> and several minor <a href="/wiki/Archipelagos" class="mw-redirect" title="Archipelagos">archipelagos</a>. Cuba is located in the northern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> meet. It is south of both the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>, west of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and north of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>. <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> is the largest city and capital; other major cities include <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey" title="Camagüey">Camagüey</a>. Cuba is the largest island in the Caribbean, with an area of 109,884 square kilometres (42,426&#160;sq&#160;mi), and the second-most populous after <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, with over 11 million inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_profile_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_profile-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to Spanish colonization in the late 15th century, Cuba was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> tribes. It remained a colony of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> of 1898, which led to <a href="/wiki/Platt_Amendment" title="Platt Amendment">nominal independence</a> as a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> protectorate in 1902. As a fragile republic, Cuba attempted to <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Constitution_of_1940" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban Constitution of 1940">strengthen its democratic system</a>, but mounting political radicalization and social strife culminated in the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a> in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> Further unrest and instability led to <a href="/wiki/Cuban_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban revolution">Batista's ousting in January 1959</a> by the <a href="/wiki/July_26_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="July 26 Movement">July 26 Movement</a>, which afterwards established a government under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>. Since 1965, the state has been governed by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party of Cuba</a>. A point of contention during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and the United States, a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear war">nuclear war</a> nearly broke out during the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> of 1962.</p>
<p>Culturally, Cuba is considered part of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic">multiethnic</a> country whose <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cuba" title="Culture of Cuba">culture</a> and customs derive from diverse origins, including the aboriginal <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taíno people">Taíno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a> peoples, the long period of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colonialism</a>, the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Spanish_New_World_colonies" title="Slavery in the Spanish New World colonies">African slaves</a>, and a close <a href="/wiki/Cuba-Soviet_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuba-Soviet relations">relationship with the Soviet Union</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.</p>
<p>Cuba is a <a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist–Leninist">Marxist–Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party republic</a>, where the role of the vanguard Communist Party is enshrined in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Cuba" title="Constitution of Cuba">Constitution</a>. Independent observers have accused the Cuban government of numerous <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses, including <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_imprisonment" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbitrary imprisonment">arbitrary imprisonment</a>. It is one of the world's last <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economies</a> and its economy is dominated by the exports of sugar, tobacco, coffee and skilled labor. According to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, Cuba is described as a country with high human development and is ranked the eighth highest in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> It also ranks highly in some metrics of national performance, including <a href="/wiki/Cuba#Health" title="Cuba">health care</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba#Education" title="Cuba">education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Cuba</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Taíno language">Taíno language</a>. The exact meaning of the name is unclear but it may be translated either as 'where fertile land is abundant' (<i>cubao</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> or 'great place' (<i>coabana</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> Authors who believe that <a href="/wiki/Origin_theories_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Origin theories of Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus was Portuguese</a> state that <i>Cuba</i> was named by Columbus for the <a href="/wiki/Cuba,_Portugal" title="Cuba, Portugal">town of Cuba</a> in the district of <a href="/wiki/Beja_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beja (Portugal)">Beja</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cuba" title="History of Cuba">History of Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Cuban_history" title="Timeline of Cuban history">Timeline of Cuban history</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatuey_monument,_Baracoa,_Cuba.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG/170px-Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG/255px-Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG/340px-Hatuey_monument%2C_Baracoa%2C_Cuba.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1515" data-file-height="2272" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatuey_monument,_Baracoa,_Cuba.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument of <a href="/wiki/Hatuey" title="Hatuey">Hatuey</a>, an early <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> chief of Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before the arrival of the Spanish, Cuba was inhabited by three distinct tribes of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples of the Americas</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taíno people">Taíno</a> (an <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a> people), the <a href="/wiki/Guanajatabey" class="mw-redirect" title="Guanajatabey">Guanajatabey</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciboney people">Ciboney people</a>.</p>
<p>The ancestors of the Ciboney migrated from the mainland of South America, with the earliest sites dated to 5,000 BP.<sup id="cite_ref-AnAofPCC_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnAofPCC-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Taíno arrived from <a href="/wiki/Hispanola" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanola">Hispanola</a> sometime in the 3rd century A.D. When Columbus arrived they were the dominant culture in Cuba, having an estimated population of 150,000.<sup id="cite_ref-AnAofPCC_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnAofPCC-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name "Cuba" comes from the native Taíno language. It is derived from either <i>coabana</i> meaning "great place," or from <i>cubao</i> meaning "where fertile land is abundant".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Taíno were farmers, while the Ciboney were farmers as well as fishers and <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonization_and_rule_.281492.E2.80.931898.29">Spanish colonization and rule (1492–1898)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Cuba" title="Captaincy General of Cuba">Captaincy General of Cuba</a></div>
<p>After first landing on an island then called <a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, on October 12, 1492,<sup id="cite_ref-Henken2008_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henken2008-28">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> commanded his three ships: <i><a href="/wiki/Pinta_(ship)" title="Pinta (ship)">La Pinta</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%B1a" title="Niña">La Niña</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">Santa María</a>,</i> to land on Cuba's northeastern coast on October 28, 1492.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> (This was near what is now Bariay, <a href="/wiki/Holgu%C3%ADn_Province" title="Holguín Province">Holguín Province</a>.) Columbus claimed the island for the new Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a><sup id="cite_ref-Gott_p13_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gott_p13-30">[29]</a></sup> and named it <i>Isla Juana</i> after <a href="/wiki/Juan,_Prince_of_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan, Prince of Asturias">Juan, Prince of Asturias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg/170px-DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg/255px-DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg/340px-DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="2075" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DiegoVelazquezCuellar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez_de_Cu%C3%A9llar" title="Diego Velázquez de Cuéllar">Diego Velázquez de Cuéllar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> of Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1511, the first Spanish settlement was founded by <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez_de_Cu%C3%A9llar" title="Diego Velázquez de Cuéllar">Diego Velázquez de Cuéllar</a> at <a href="/wiki/Baracoa" title="Baracoa">Baracoa</a>. Other towns soon followed, including <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">San Cristobal de la Habana</a>, founded in 1515, which later became the capital. The native Taíno were forced to work under the <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a> system,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> which resembled a <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudal system</a> in Medieval Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-McAlister_1984_164_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McAlister_1984_164-33">[32]</a></sup> Within a century the indigenous people were virtually wiped out due to multiple factors, primarily Eurasian <a href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a>, to which they had no natural resistance (immunity), aggravated by harsh conditions of the repressive colonial subjugation.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> In 1529, a <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a> outbreak in Cuba killed two-thirds of those few natives who had previously survived <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 18, 1539, Conquistador <a href="/wiki/Hernando_de_Soto" title="Hernando de Soto">Hernando de Soto</a> departed from Havana, Cuba at the head of some 600 followers into a vast expedition through the Southeastern United States, starting at La <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, in search of gold, treasure, fame and power.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> On September 1, 1548, Dr. Gonzalo Perez de Angulo was appointed governor of Cuba. He arrived in Santiago, Cuba on November 4, 1549 and immediately declared the liberty of all natives.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright_1916_183_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_1916_183-38">[37]</a></sup> He became Cuba's first permanent governor to reside in Havana instead of Santiago, and he built Havana's first church made of masonry.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright_1916_229_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_1916_229-39">[38]</a></sup> After the French took Havana in 1555, the governor's son, Francisco de Angulo, went to Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright_1916_246_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_1916_246-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba developed slowly and, unlike the plantation islands of the Caribbean, had a diversified agriculture. But what was most important was that the colony developed as an urbanized society that primarily supported the Spanish colonial empire. By the mid-18th century, its colonists held 50,000 slaves, compared to 60,000 in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>; 300,000 in <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Virginia</a>, both British colonies; and 450,000 in French <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, which had large-scale sugar cane plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6234" data-file-height="4799" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Descriptionis_Ptolemaic%C3%A6_avgmentvm_siue_Occidentis_notitia_breui_commentario_illustrata_p193.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Cuba by Cornelius van Wytfliet in 1597 (National Library of Sweden)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, which erupted in 1754 across three continents, eventually arrived in the Spanish Caribbean. Spain's alliance with the French pitched them into direct conflict with the British, and in 1762 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Havana_(1762)" title="Battle of Havana (1762)">a British expedition</a> of five warships and 4,000 troops set out from <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> to capture Cuba. The British arrived on June 6, and by August had Havana under <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">siege</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Siege_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Siege-42">[41]</a></sup> When Havana surrendered, the admiral of the British fleet, <a href="/wiki/George_Keppel,_3rd_Earl_of_Albemarle" title="George Keppel, 3rd Earl of Albemarle">George Keppel</a>, the 3rd <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Albemarle" title="Earl of Albemarle">Earl of Albemarle</a>, entered the city as a conquering new governor and took control of the whole western part of the island. The British immediately opened up trade with their North American and Caribbean colonies, causing a rapid transformation of Cuban society. They imported food, horses and other goods into the city, as well as thousands of slaves from West Africa to work on the under developed sugar plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-Siege_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Siege-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/220px-LindsayCambridge.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/330px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/440px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="952" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Cuba">British invasion and occupation of Havana</a> in 1762</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though Havana, which had become the third-largest city in the Americas, was to enter an era of sustained development and increasing ties with North America during this period, the British occupation of the city proved short-lived. Pressure from London sugar merchants, fearing a decline in sugar prices, forced negotiations with the Spanish over colonial territories. Less than a year after Britain seized Havana, it signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Peace of Paris</a> together with France and Spain, ending the Seven Years' War. The treaty gave Britain <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> in exchange for Cuba. The French had recommended this to Spain, advising that declining to give up Florida could result in Spain instead losing Mexico and much of the South American mainland to the British.<sup id="cite_ref-Siege_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Siege-42">[41]</a></sup> Many in Britain were disappointed, believing that Florida was a poor return for Cuba and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_in_the_Seven_Years%27_War" title="Great Britain in the Seven Years' War">Britain's other gains in the war</a>.</p>
<p>The real engine for the growth of Cuba's commerce in the late eighteenth and early nineteenth century was the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a>. When the enslaved peoples of what had been the Caribbean's richest colony freed themselves through violent revolt, Cuban planters perceived the region's changing circumstances with both a sense of fear and opportunity. They were afraid because of the prospect that slaves might revolt in Cuba, too, and numerous prohibitions during the 1790s on the sale of slaves in Cuba that had previously been slaves in French colonies underscored this anxiety. The planters saw opportunity, however, because they thought that they could exploit the situation by transforming Cuba into the slave society and sugar-producing "pearl of the Antilles" that Haiti had been before the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> As the historian Ada Ferrer has written, "At a basic level, liberation in Saint-Domingue helped entrench its denial in Cuba. As slavery and colonialism collapsed in the French colony, the Spanish island underwent transformations that were almost the mirror image of Haiti's."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Estimates suggest that between 1790 and 1820 some 325,000 Africans were imported to Cuba as slaves, which was four times the amount that had arrived between 1760 and 1790.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg/220px-Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg/330px-Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg/440px-Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2382" data-file-height="1539" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slaves_Unloading_Ice_in_Cuba_1832.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slaves</a> in Cuba unloading ice from Maine, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1832</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although a smaller proportion of the population of Cuba was enslaved, at times slaves arose in revolt. In 1812 the Aponte Slave Rebellion took place but it was suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The population of Cuba in 1817 was 630,980, of which 291,021 were white, 115,691 <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> (mixed-race), and 224,268 black slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Scheina_2003_352_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scheina_2003_352-47">[46]</a></sup> This was a much higher proportion of free blacks to slaves than in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, for instance, or the other Caribbean islands. Historians such as Swedish Magnus Mõrner, who studied slavery in Latin America, found that <a href="/wiki/Manumission" title="Manumission">manumissions</a> increased when slave economies were in decline, as in 18th-century Cuba and early 19th-century Maryland of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In part due to Cuban slaves working primarily in urbanized settings, by the 19th century, there had developed the practice of <i>coartacion</i>, or "buying oneself out of slavery", a "uniquely Cuban development", according to historian Herbert S. Klein.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Due to a shortage of white labor, blacks dominated urban industries "to such an extent that when whites in large numbers came to Cuba in the middle of the nineteenth century, they were unable to displace Negro workers."<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup> A system of diversified agriculture, with small farms and fewer slaves, served to supply the cities with produce and other goods.<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1820s, when the rest of Spain's empire in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> rebelled and formed independent states, Cuba remained loyal. Its economy was based on serving the empire. By 1860, Cuba had 213,167 free people of color, 39% of its non-White population of 550,000.<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup> By contrast, Virginia with about the same number of blacks, had only 58,042 or 11% who were free; the rest were enslaved.<sup id="cite_ref-drimmer_41-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drimmer-41">[40]</a></sup> In the antebellum years, Virginia discouraged manumissions after the <a href="/wiki/Nat_Turner%27s_Slave_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Nat Turner's Slave Rebellion">Nat Turner's Slave Rebellion</a> of 1831 and strengthened restrictions against free blacks, as did other southern states. In addition, there was a high demand for slaves, and Virginia planters sold many in the internal domestic slave trade, to be shipped or taken overland to the Deep South, which had greatly expanded its cotton production.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_movements">Independence movements</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">Cuban War of Independence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg/170px-Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg/255px-Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg/340px-Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="391" data-file-height="580" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_Manuel_de_Cespedes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Carlos_Manuel_de_C%C3%A9spedes" title="Carlos Manuel de Céspedes">Carlos Manuel de Céspedes</a> is known as <i>Father of the Homeland</i> in Cuba, having declared the nation's independence from Spain in 1868.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Full independence from Spain was the goal of a rebellion in 1868 led by planter <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Manuel_de_C%C3%A9spedes" title="Carlos Manuel de Céspedes">Carlos Manuel de Céspedes</a>. De Céspedes, a sugar planter, freed his slaves to fight with him for an independent Cuba. On December 27, 1868, he issued a decree condemning slavery in theory but accepting it in practice and declaring free any slaves whose masters present them for military service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChomskyCarrSmorkaloff2004.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DSr2hQkCIihMC.26pg.3DPA115_115.E2.80.937.5D_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChomskyCarrSmorkaloff2004.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DSr2hQkCIihMC.26pg.3DPA115_115.E2.80.937.5D-50">[49]</a></sup> The 1868 rebellion resulted in a prolonged conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Years%27_War" title="Ten Years' War">Ten Years' War</a>. Two thousand Cuban Chinese joined the rebels. Chinese had been imported as indentured laborers. A monument in Havana honours the Cuban Chinese who fell in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States declined to recognize the new Cuban government, although many European and Latin American nations did so.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> In 1878, the <a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Zanj%C3%B3n" title="Pact of Zanjón">Pact of Zanjón</a> ended the conflict, with Spain promising greater autonomy to Cuba. In 1879–1880, Cuban patriot <a href="/wiki/Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Calixto García">Calixto García</a> attempted to start another war known as the <a href="/wiki/Little_War_(Cuba)" title="Little War (Cuba)">Little War</a> but did not receive enough support.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Cuba" title="Slavery in Cuba">Slavery in Cuba</a> was abolished in 1875 but the process was completed only in 1886.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott_2000_3_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott_2000_3-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChomskyCarrSmorkaloff2004.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DSr2hQkCIihMC.26pg.3DPA37_37.E2.80.938.5D_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChomskyCarrSmorkaloff2004.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DSr2hQkCIihMC.26pg.3DPA37_37.E2.80.938.5D-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>An exiled dissident named <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">José Martí</a> founded the Cuban Revolutionary Party in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> in 1892. The aim of the party was to achieve Cuban independence from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-sandler_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandler-56">[55]</a></sup> In January 1895 Martí traveled to <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando_de_Monte_Cristi" class="mw-redirect" title="San Fernando de Monte Cristi">Montecristi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> to join the efforts of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ximo_G%C3%B3mez" title="Máximo Gómez">Máximo Gómez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sandler_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandler-56">[55]</a></sup> Martí recorded his political views in the <i><a href="/wiki/Manifesto_of_Montecristi" title="Manifesto of Montecristi">Manifesto of Montecristi</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-arias_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arias-57">[56]</a></sup> Fighting against the Spanish army began in Cuba on February 24, 1895, but Martí was unable to reach Cuba until April 11, 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-sandler_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandler-56">[55]</a></sup> Martí was killed in the battle of Dos Rios on May 19, 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-sandler_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandler-56">[55]</a></sup> His death immortalized him as Cuba's national hero.<sup id="cite_ref-arias_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arias-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba,_1898.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg/220px-Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg/330px-Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg/440px-Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba%2C_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="912" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa_and_William_Ludlow_in_Cuba,_1898.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Calixto_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Calixto García">Calixto García</a>, a general of Cuban separatist rebels, (right) with U.S. Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/William_Ludlow" title="William Ludlow">William Ludlow</a> (Cuba, 1898)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Around 200,000 Spanish troops outnumbered the much smaller rebel army, which relied mostly on <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sabotage" title="Sabotage">sabotage</a> tactics. The Spaniards began a campaign of suppression. General <a href="/wiki/Valeriano_Weyler" title="Valeriano Weyler">Valeriano Weyler</a>, military governor of Cuba, herded the rural population into what he called <i>reconcentrados</i>, described by international observers as "fortified towns". These are often considered the prototype for 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Between 200,000 and 400,000 Cuban civilians died from starvation and disease in the camps, numbers verified by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> and United States Senator <a href="/wiki/Redfield_Proctor" title="Redfield Proctor">Redfield Proctor</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War" title="United States Secretary of War">Secretary of War</a>. American and European protests against Spanish conduct on the island followed.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. battleship <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">Maine</a></i> was sent to protect U.S. interests, but soon after arrival, it exploded in Havana harbor and sank quickly, killing nearly three quarters of the crew. The cause and responsibility for the sinking of the ship remained unclear after a board of inquiry. Popular opinion in the U.S., fueled by an active press, concluded that the Spanish were to blame and demanded action.<sup id="cite_ref-morison_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morison-60">[59]</a></sup> Spain and the United States declared war on each other in late April 1898.</p>
<p>Over the decades, five U.S. presidents—<a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">Polk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce" title="Franklin Pierce">Pierce</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">Buchanan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Grant</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">McKinley</a>—had tried to buy the island of Cuba from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-Falk_1998_64_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falk_1998_64-61">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281902.E2.80.9359.29">Independence (1902–59)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cuba_(1902%E2%80%9359)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Cuba (1902–59)">History of Cuba (1902–59)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20,_1902.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif/220px-Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif/330px-Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif/440px-Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20%2C_1902.gif 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raising_the_Cuban_flag_on_the_Governor_General%27s_Palace_at_noon_on_May_20,_1902.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Raising the Cuban flag on the Governor General's Palace at noon on May 20, 1902</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, Spain and the United States signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris (1898)</a>, by which Spain ceded <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> to the United States for the sum of <span class="nowrap">US$20 million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> Cuba gained formal independence from the U.S. on May 20, 1902, as the Republic of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-P.C3.A9rez1998_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-P.C3.A9rez1998-64">[63]</a></sup> Under Cuba's new constitution, the U.S. retained the right to intervene in Cuban affairs and to supervise its finances and foreign relations. Under the <a href="/wiki/Platt_Amendment" title="Platt Amendment">Platt Amendment</a>, the U.S. leased the <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay" title="Guantánamo Bay">Guantánamo Bay</a> naval base from Cuba.</p>
<p>Following disputed elections in 1906, the first president, <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Estrada_Palma" title="Tomás Estrada Palma">Tomás Estrada Palma</a>, faced an armed revolt by independence war veterans who defeated the meager government forces.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The U.S. intervened by occupying Cuba and named <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Magoon" title="Charles Edward Magoon">Charles Edward Magoon</a> as Governor for three years. Cuban historians have characterized Magoon's governorship as having introduced political and social corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_1998_283to287_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_1998_283to287-66">[65]</a></sup> In 1908, self-government was restored when <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_G%C3%B3mez" title="José Miguel Gómez">José Miguel Gómez</a> was elected President, but the U.S. continued intervening in Cuban affairs. In 1912, the <a href="/wiki/Partido_Independiente_de_Color" title="Partido Independiente de Color">Partido Independiente de Color</a> attempted to establish a separate black republic in Oriente Province,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> but was suppressed by General Monteagudo with considerable bloodshed.</p>
<p>In 1924, <a href="/wiki/Gerardo_Machado" title="Gerardo Machado">Gerardo Machado</a> was elected president.<sup id="cite_ref-D2012_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D2012-68">[67]</a></sup> During his administration, tourism increased markedly, and American-owned hotels and restaurants were built to accommodate the influx of tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-D2012_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D2012-68">[67]</a></sup> The tourist boom led to increases in gambling and prostitution.<sup id="cite_ref-D2012_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D2012-68">[67]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a> led to a collapse in the price of sugar, political unrest, and repression.<sup id="cite_ref-ChaffeePrevost1992_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChaffeePrevost1992-69">[68]</a></sup> Protesting students, known as the Generation of 1930, turned to violence in opposition to the increasingly unpopular Machado.<sup id="cite_ref-ChaffeePrevost1992_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChaffeePrevost1992-69">[68]</a></sup> A general strike (in which the Communist Party sided with Machado),<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> uprisings among sugar workers, and an army revolt forced Machado into exile in August 1933. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Manuel_de_C%C3%A9spedes_y_Quesada" title="Carlos Manuel de Céspedes y Quesada">Carlos Manuel de Céspedes y Quesada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChaffeePrevost1992_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChaffeePrevost1992-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg/220px-1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg/330px-1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg/440px-1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="611" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1933-Pentarchy_w_Batista.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Pentarchy_of_1933" title="Pentarchy of 1933">Pentarchy of 1933</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, who controlled the armed forces, appears at far right</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In September 1933, the Sergeants' Revolt, led by Sergeant <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, overthrew Cespedes.<sup id="cite_ref-MJ303_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MJ303-71">[70]</a></sup> A five-member executive committee (the <a href="/wiki/Pentarchy_of_1933" title="Pentarchy of 1933">Pentarchy of 1933</a>) was chosen to head a provisional government.<sup id="cite_ref-Suchlicki2002_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suchlicki2002-72">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Grau_San_Mart%C3%ADn" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramón Grau San Martín">Ramón Grau San Martín</a> was then appointed as provisional president.<sup id="cite_ref-Suchlicki2002_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suchlicki2002-72">[71]</a></sup> Grau resigned in 1934, leaving the way clear for Batista, who dominated Cuban politics for the next 25 years, at first through a series of puppet-presidents.<sup id="cite_ref-MJ303_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MJ303-71">[70]</a></sup> The period from 1933 to 1937 was a time of "virtually unremitting social and political warfare".<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_76_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_76-73">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/1940_Constitution_of_Cuba" title="1940 Constitution of Cuba">new constitution</a> was adopted in 1940, which engineered radical progressive ideas, including the right to labour and health care.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_.3F_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_.3F-74">[73]</a></sup> Batista was elected president in the same year, holding the post until 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-Villafana2011_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villafana2011-75">[74]</a></sup> He is so far the only non-white Cuban to win the nation's highest political office.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_1988_662_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz_1988_662-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bethell_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bethell-77">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sweig_2004_4_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sweig_2004_4-78">[77]</a></sup> His government carried out major social reforms. Several members of the Communist Party held office under his administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Sweig_2004_.3F_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sweig_2004_.3F-79">[78]</a></sup> Cuban armed forces were not greatly involved in combat during World War&#160;II, although president Batista suggested a joint U.S.-Latin American assault on <a href="/wiki/Spanish_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish State">Francoist Spain</a> in order to overthrow its <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> regime.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Batista adhered to the 1940 constitution's strictures preventing his re-election.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_101_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_101-81">[80]</a></sup> Ramon Grau San Martin was the winner of the next election, in 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-Villafana2011_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villafana2011-75">[74]</a></sup> Grau further corroded the base of the already teetering legitimacy of the Cuban political system, in particular by undermining the deeply flawed, though not entirely ineffectual, Congress and Supreme Court.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_110_111_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1978_110_111-82">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pr%C3%ADo_Socarr%C3%A1s" title="Carlos Prío Socarrás">Carlos Prío Socarrás</a>, a protégé of Grau, became president in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-Villafana2011_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villafana2011-75">[74]</a></sup> The two terms of the Auténtico Party saw an influx of investment which fueled a boom and raised living standards for all segments of society and created a prosperous middle class in most urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Alvarez_2004_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alvarez_2004-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HavanaSlums1954.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/HavanaSlums1954.jpg/210px-HavanaSlums1954.jpg" width="210" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/HavanaSlums1954.jpg/315px-HavanaSlums1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/HavanaSlums1954.jpg/420px-HavanaSlums1954.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HavanaSlums1954.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">Slum</a> (<i>bohio</i>) dwellings in Havana, Cuba in 1954, just outside <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Latinoamericano" title="Estadio Latinoamericano">Havana baseball stadium</a>. In the background is advertising for a nearby <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After running unsuccessfully for the presidency in 1952, Batista staged a coup.<sup id="cite_ref-IhrieOropesa2011_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IhrieOropesa2011-84">[83]</a></sup> He outlawed the Cuban Communist Party in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-Sweig_2004_6_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sweig_2004_6-85">[84]</a></sup> After the coup, Cuba had Latin America's highest per capita consumption rates of meat, vegetables, cereals, automobiles, telephones and radios, though about one third of the population was considered poor and enjoyed relatively little of this consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-lewis_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lewis-86">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1958, Cuba was a relatively well-advanced country by Latin American standards, and in some cases by world standards.<sup id="cite_ref-asce_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asce-87">[86]</a></sup> On the other hand, Cuba was affected by perhaps the largest labor union privileges in Latin America, including bans on dismissals and mechanization. They were obtained in large measure "at the cost of the unemployed and the peasants", leading to disparities.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Between 1933 and 1958, Cuba extended economic regulations enormously, causing economic problems.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_1988_662_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz_1988_662-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_1998_1173_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_1998_1173-89">[88]</a></sup> Unemployment became a problem as graduates entering the workforce could not find jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_1988_662_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz_1988_662-76">[75]</a></sup> The middle class, which was comparable to that of the United States, became increasingly dissatisfied with unemployment and political persecution. The labor unions supported Batista until the very end.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz_1988_662_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz_1988_662-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bethell_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bethell-77">[76]</a></sup> Batista stayed in power until he was forced into exile in December 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-IhrieOropesa2011_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IhrieOropesa2011-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_Communist_party_rule_.281959.E2.80.93present.29">Revolution and Communist party rule (1959–present)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/170px-CheyFidel.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/255px-CheyFidel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/340px-CheyFidel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1197" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, photographed by <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Korda" title="Alberto Korda">Alberto Korda</a> in 1961</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1950s, various organizations, including some advocating armed uprising, competed for public support in bringing about political change.<sup id="cite_ref-Chomsky2010_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chomsky2010-90">[89]</a></sup> In 1956, <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> and about 80 supporters landed from the yacht <a href="/wiki/Granma_(yacht)" title="Granma (yacht)"><i>Granma</i></a> in an attempt to start a rebellion against the Batista government.<sup id="cite_ref-Chomsky2010_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chomsky2010-90">[89]</a></sup> It was not until 1958 that Castro's <a href="/wiki/July_26th_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="July 26th Movement">July 26th Movement</a> emerged as the leading revolutionary group.<sup id="cite_ref-Chomsky2010_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chomsky2010-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>By late 1958 the rebels had broken out of the Sierra Maestra and launched a general popular insurrection. After Castro's fighters captured <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_Cuba" title="Santa Clara, Cuba">Santa Clara</a>, Batista fled with his family to the Dominican Republic on January 1, 1959. Later he went into exile on the Portuguese island of Madeira and finally settled in Estoril, near Lisbon. Fidel Castro's forces entered the capital on January 8, 1959. The liberal <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Urrutia_Lle%C3%B3" title="Manuel Urrutia Lleó">Manuel Urrutia Lleó</a> became the provisional president.<sup id="cite_ref-Falk_1988_67_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falk_1988_67-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1959 to 1966 Cuban insurgents fought a <a href="/wiki/War_against_the_Bandits" class="mw-redirect" title="War against the Bandits">six-year rebellion</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Escambray_Mountains" title="Escambray Mountains">Escambray Mountains</a> against the Castro government. The government's vastly superior numbers eventually crushed the insurgency. The rebellion lasted longer and involved more soldiers than the Cuban Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-Ros_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ros-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cuba_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cuba-93">[92]</a></sup> The U.S. State Department has estimated that 3,200 people were executed from 1959 to 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, death sentences from 1959–87 numbered 237 of which all but 21 were actually carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> Other estimates for the total number of political executions range from 4,000 to 33,000.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Power_Kills_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Kills-97">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> The vast majority of those executed following the 1959 revolution were policemen, politicians, and informers of the Batista regime accused of crimes such as torture and murder, and their public trials and executions had widespread popular support among the Cuban population.<sup id="cite_ref-Chase_2010_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chase_2010-99">[98]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg/220px-Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg/330px-Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg/440px-Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="1150" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guantanamo_Naval_Base_aerial_photo_1962.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Since 1959, Cuba regards the U.S. presence in <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">Guantánamo Bay</a> as illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United States government initially reacted favorably to the Cuban revolution, seeing it as part of a movement to bring democracy to Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-Rabe1988_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabe1988-101">[100]</a></sup> Castro's legalization of the Communist party and the hundreds of executions that followed caused a deterioration in the relationship between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Rabe1988_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabe1988-101">[100]</a></sup> The promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_Reform_Laws_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Agrarian Reform Laws of Cuba">Agrarian Reform Law</a>, expropriating thousands of acres of farmland (including from large U.S. landholders), further worsened relations.<sup id="cite_ref-Rabe1988_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabe1988-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crooker2005_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crooker2005-102">[101]</a></sup> In response, between 1960 and 1964 the U.S imposed a range of sanctions, eventually including a total ban on trade between the countries and a freeze on all Cuban-owned assets in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-Commission_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission-103">[102]</a></sup> In February 1960, Castro signed a commercial agreement with Soviet Vice-Premier <a href="/wiki/Anastas_Mikoyan" title="Anastas Mikoyan">Anastas Mikoyan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rabe1988_101-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabe1988-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1960, Eisenhower gave his approval to a CIA plan to arm and train a group of Cuban refugees to overthrow the Castro regime.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> The invasion (known as the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</a>) took place on April 14, 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-Crooker2005_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crooker2005-102">[101]</a></sup> About 1,400 Cuban exiles disembarked at the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs" title="Bay of Pigs">Bay of Pigs</a>, but failed in their attempt to overthrow Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-Crooker2005_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crooker2005-102">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 1962, Cuba was suspended from the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS), and later the same year the OAS started to impose sanctions against Cuba of similar nature to the US sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson-105">[104]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> occurred in October 1962. By 1963, Cuba was moving towards a full-fledged Communist system modeled on the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040,_Berlin,_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040%2C_Berlin%2C_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="776" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040,_Berlin,_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fidel Castro and members of the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East German</a> <a href="/wiki/Politburo" title="Politburo">Politburo</a> in 1972</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 1970s, Fidel Castro dispatched tens of thousands of troops in support of Soviet-supported wars in Africa. He supported the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola">MPLA</a> in <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mengistu_Haile_Mariam" title="Mengistu Haile Mariam">Mengistu Haile Mariam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_.3F_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_.3F-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The standard of living in the 1970s was "extremely spartan" and discontent was rife.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-108">[107]</a></sup> Fidel Castro admitted the failures of economic policies in a 1970 speech.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-108">[107]</a></sup> In 1975 the OAS lifted its sanctions against Cuba, with the approval of 16 member states, including the U.S. The U.S., however, maintained its own sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Castro's rule was severely tested in the aftermath of the Soviet collapse in 1991 (known in Cuba as the <a href="/wiki/Special_Period" title="Special Period">Special Period</a>). The country faced a severe economic downturn following the withdrawal of Soviet subsidies worth <span class="nowrap">$4 billion</span> to <span class="nowrap">$6 billion</span> annually, resulting in effects such as food and fuel shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-cmaj_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmaj-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> The government did not accept American donations of food, medicines, and cash until 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-cmaj_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmaj-109">[108]</a></sup> On August 5, 1994, state security dispersed protesters in a <a href="/wiki/Maleconazo_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Maleconazo uprising">spontaneous protest</a> in Havana.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FidelCastro645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/FidelCastro645.jpg/220px-FidelCastro645.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/FidelCastro645.jpg/330px-FidelCastro645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/FidelCastro645.jpg/440px-FidelCastro645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1801" data-file-height="1181" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FidelCastro645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fidel Castro with South African president <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a> and the Swedish prime minister <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ran_Persson" title="Göran Persson">Göran Persson</a>, 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuba has since found a new source of aid and support in the People's Republic of China. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a>, former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Venezuela" title="President of Venezuela">President of Venezuela</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">President of Bolivia</a>, became allies and both countries are major oil and gas exporters. In 2003, the government arrested and imprisoned a large number of civil activists, a period known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Spring_(Cuba)" title="Black Spring (Cuba)">"Black Spring"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2008, Fidel Castro announced his resignation as President of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> On February 24 his brother, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">Raúl Castro</a>, was declared the new President.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> In his inauguration speech, Raúl promised that some of the restrictions on freedom in Cuba would be removed.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> In March 2009, Raúl Castro removed some of <a href="/wiki/2009_Cuban_government_dismissals" title="2009 Cuban government dismissals">his brother's appointees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 3, 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> adopted a resolution to end the 47-year ban on Cuban membership of the group.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> The resolution stated, however, that full membership would be delayed until Cuba was "in conformity with the practices, purposes, and principles of the OAS".<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson-105">[104]</a></sup> Fidel Castro restated his position that he was not interested in joining after the OAS resolution had been announced.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png/220px-President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png/330px-President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png/440px-President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="638" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Meets_with_President_Castro.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Raúl Castro meets with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Panama, April 11, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Effective January 14, 2013, Cuba ended the requirement established in 1961, that any citizens who wish to travel abroad were required to obtain an expensive government permit and a letter of invitation.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> In 1961 the Cuban government had imposed broad restrictions on travel to prevent the mass emigration of people after the 1959 revolution;<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> it approved exit visas only on rare occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Requirements were simplified: Cubans need only a passport and a national ID card to leave; and they are allowed to take their young children with them for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> However, a passport costs on average five months' salary. Observers expect that Cubans with paying relatives abroad are most likely to be able to take advantage of the new policy.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> In the first year of the program, over 180,000 left Cuba and returned.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of December 2014, talks with Cuban officials and American officials including President Barack Obama have resulted in the exchange of releasing <a href="/wiki/Alan_Gross" title="Alan Gross">Alan Gross</a>, fifty-two political prisoners, and an unnamed non-citizen agent of the United States in return for the release of three Cuban agents currently imprisoned in the United States. Additionally, while the embargo between the United States and Cuba will not be immediately lifted, it will be relaxed to allow import, export, and certain commerce within a limit between the two.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cuba" title="Politics of Cuba">Politics of Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CubaElectio.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CubaElectio.JPG/220px-CubaElectio.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CubaElectio.JPG/330px-CubaElectio.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/CubaElectio.JPG/440px-CubaElectio.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CubaElectio.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sign promoting the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_parliamentary_election,_2008" title="Cuban parliamentary election, 2008">2008 parliamentary election</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Republic of Cuba is one of the world's last remaining <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> countries following the <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> ideology. The Constitution of 1976, which defined Cuba as a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist republic">socialist republic</a>, was replaced by the Constitution of 1992, which is "guided by the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">José Martí</a> and the political and social ideas of <a href="/wiki/Marx" class="mw-redirect" title="Marx">Marx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Engels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lenin" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenin">Lenin</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup> The constitution describes the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party of Cuba</a> as the "leading force of society and of the state".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="First Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba">First Secretary of the Communist Party</a> is concurrently President of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of State of Cuba">Council of State</a> (<a href="/wiki/President_of_Cuba" title="President of Cuba">President of Cuba</a>) and President of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of Cuba">Council of Ministers</a> (sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Cuba">Premier of Cuba</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> Members of both councils are elected by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_People%27s_Power" title="National Assembly of People's Power">National Assembly of People's Power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup> The President of Cuba, who is also elected by the Assembly, serves for five years and there is no limit to the number of terms of office.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg/220px-Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg/330px-Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg/440px-Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="1584" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comit%C3%A9_Central_PCC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Supreme_Court_of_Cuba" title="People's Supreme Court of Cuba">People's Supreme Court</a> serves as Cuba's highest judicial branch of government. It is also the court of last resort for all appeals against the decisions of provincial courts.</p>
<p>Cuba's national legislature, the National Assembly of People's Power (<i>Asamblea Nacional de Poder Popular</i>), is the supreme organ of power; 609 members serve five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup> The assembly meets twice a year; between sessions legislative power is held by the 31 member Council of Ministers. Candidates for the Assembly are approved by public referendum. All Cuban citizens over 16 who have not been convicted of a criminal offense can vote.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> Article 131 of the Constitution states that voting shall be "through free, equal and secret vote".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup> Article 136 states: "In order for deputies or delegates to be considered elected they must get more than half the number of valid votes cast in the electoral districts".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>No <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Cuba" title="List of political parties in Cuba">political party</a> is permitted to nominate candidates or campaign on the island, including the Communist Party.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> The Communist Party of Cuba has held six party congress meetings since 1975. In 2011, the party stated that there were 800,000 members, and representatives generally constitute at least half of the Councils of state and the National Assembly. The remaining positions are filled by candidates nominally without party affiliation. Other political parties campaign and raise finances internationally, while activity within Cuba by <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_Fidel_Castro" class="mw-redirect" title="Opposition to Fidel Castro">opposition groups</a> is minimal.</p>
<p>In February 2013, Raúl Castro, current Cuban President, announced his resignation for 2018, that will end his current 5-year term, and hope to implement permanent term limits for future Cuban Presidents, including age limits.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the death of Fidel Castro on November 25, 2016 the Cuban government put in place a nine-day mourning period. During the mourning period Cuban citizens were prohibited from playing loud music, partying, and drinking alcohol.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Cuba" title="Provinces of Cuba">Provinces of Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Cuba" title="Municipalities of Cuba">Municipalities of Cuba</a></div>
<p>The country is subdivided into 15 provinces and one special municipality (Isla de la Juventud). These were formerly part of six larger historical provinces: Pinar del Río, Habana, Matanzas, Las Villas, Camagüey and Oriente. The present subdivisions closely resemble those of the Spanish military provinces during the Cuban Wars of Independence, when the most troublesome areas were subdivided. The provinces are divided into municipalities.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CubaSubdivisions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/CubaSubdivisions.png/440px-CubaSubdivisions.png" width="440" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/CubaSubdivisions.png/660px-CubaSubdivisions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/CubaSubdivisions.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="339" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CubaSubdivisions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Provinces of Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a></li>
