<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Cuba" title="Human rights in Cuba">Human rights in Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_Cuba" title="Censorship in Cuba">Censorship in Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cuban_dissidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban dissidents">Cuban dissidents</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana,_Cuba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg/220px-Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg/330px-Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg/440px-Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana%2C_Cuba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1787" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Damas_de_Blanco_demonstration_in_Havana,_Cuba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ladies_in_White" title="Ladies in White">Ladies in White</a> demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> (April 2012)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cuban government has been accused of numerous <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights abuse">human rights abuses</a> including <a href="/wiki/Torture_in_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Torture in Cuba">torture</a>, arbitrary imprisonment, unfair trials, and extrajudicial executions (also known as "<i>El Paredón</i>").<sup id="cite_ref-cidh_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cidh-134">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has stated that the government "represses nearly all forms of political dissent" and that "Cubans are systematically denied basic rights to free expression, association, assembly, privacy, movement, and due process of law".<sup id="cite_ref-hrw2006_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw2006-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) accused the Cuban government of "continuing flagrant violation of human rights and fundamental freedoms".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> It has continued to call regularly for social and economic reform in Cuba, along with the unconditional release of all <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Political prisoners">political prisoners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Laursen_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laursen-138">[137]</a></sup> The United States continues an <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">embargo</a> against Cuba "so long as it continues to refuse to move toward democratization and greater respect for human rights",<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> though the <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> has, since 1992, passed a resolution every year condemning the ongoing impact of the embargo and claiming it to be in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a> and international law.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> Cuba considers the embargo itself to be in violation of human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> On December 17, 2014, United States President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> announced the re-establishment of diplomatic relations with Cuba, pushing for Congress to put an end to the embargo.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba had the second-highest number of imprisoned journalists of any nation in 2008 (<a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> had the highest) according to various sources, including the <a href="/wiki/Committee_to_Protect_Journalists" title="Committee to Protect Journalists">Committee to Protect Journalists</a> and Human Rights Watch.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cuban_dissidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban dissidents">Cuban dissidents</a> face arrest and imprisonment. In the 1990s, Human Rights Watch reported that Cuba's extensive prison system, one of the largest in Latin America, consists of 40 maximum-security prisons, 30 minimum-security prisons, and over 200 work camps.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw1999_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw1999-145">[144]</a></sup> According to Human Rights Watch, Cuba's prison population is confined in "substandard and unhealthy conditions, where prisoners face physical and sexual abuse".<sup id="cite_ref-hrw1999_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw1999-145">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2010, the unofficial Cuban Human Rights Commission said there were 167 political prisoners in Cuba, a fall from 201 at the start of the year. The head of the commission stated that long prison sentences were being replaced by harassment and intimidation.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cuba" title="Foreign relations of Cuba">Foreign relations of Cuba</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_medical_internationalism" title="Cuban medical internationalism">Cuban medical internationalism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Havana11.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Havana11.JPG/220px-Havana11.JPG" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Havana11.JPG/330px-Havana11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Havana11.JPG/440px-Havana11.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1480" data-file-height="904" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Havana11.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Propaganda sign in front of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Interests_Section_in_Havana" title="United States Interests Section in Havana">United States Interests Section in Havana</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuba under Castro was heavily involved in wars in Africa, Central America and Asia.</p>
<p>Cuba supported <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> in 1961–1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_1996_159.2C161_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_1996_159.2C161-147">[146]</a></sup> Cuba sent tens of thousands of troops to <a href="/wiki/Cuban_intervention_in_Angola" title="Cuban intervention in Angola">Angola</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_2010_327_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_2010_327-148">[147]</a></sup> Other countries that featured Cuban involvement include <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_2002_392_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_2002_392-149">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tareke_2009_62to63_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tareke_2009_62to63-150">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_1997_50_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_1997_50-151">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_1997_45_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_1997_45-152">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gleijeses_2002_227_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleijeses_2002_227-153">[152]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamazani1975.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D7ETnbmUmxoUC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamazani1975.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D7ETnbmUmxoUC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D-154">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba has conducted a foreign policy that is uncharacteristic of such a minor, developing country.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_6_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_6-155">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feinsilver_1989_2_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feinsilver_1989_2-156">[155]</a></sup> Lesser known actions include the 1959 missions to the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> The expedition failed, but a prominent monument to its members was erected in their memory in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> by the Dominican government, and they feature prominently at the country's Memorial Museum of the Resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> At the end of 2012, tens of thousands of Cuban medical personnel worked abroad,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> with as many as 30,000 doctors in Venezuela alone via the two countries' oil-for-doctors programme.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1996, the United States, then under President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, brought in the Cuban Liberty and Democratic Solidarity Act, better known as the <a href="/wiki/Helms%E2%80%93Burton_Act" title="Helms–Burton Act">Helms–Burton Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_42.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Raúl Castro with Mongolian President <a href="/wiki/Tsakhiagiin_Elbegdorj" title="Tsakhiagiin Elbegdorj">Elbegdorj</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2015_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade" title="2015 Moscow Victory Day Parade">Moscow Victory Day Parade</a>, May 9, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2008, the EU and Cuba agreed to resume full relations and cooperation activities.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> United States President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> stated on April 17, 2009, in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> that "the United States seeks a new beginning with Cuba",<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> and reversed the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush Administration</a>'s prohibition on travel and remittances by Cuban-Americans from the United States to Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 17, 2014, an agreement between the United States and Cuba, popularly called "The <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Thaw" title="Cuban Thaw">Cuban Thaw</a>", brokered in part by <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>, began the process of restoring international relations between Cuba and the United States. Cuba and the US agreed to release political prisoners and the United States began the process of creating an embassy in Havana.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 14, 2015, the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> announced President Obama will remove Cuba from the American government's list of nations which sponsor terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> The Cuban government has reportedly welcomed the decision as "fair".<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 30, 2015, Cuba and the U.S. reached a deal to reopen embassies in their respective capitals on July 20, 2015<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> and reestablish diplomatic relations.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">Crime and law enforcement</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Cuba" title="Law enforcement in Cuba">Law enforcement in Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Cuba" title="Crime in Cuba">Crime in Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuba_police_car_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cuba_police_car_01.JPG/220px-Cuba_police_car_01.JPG" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cuba_police_car_01.JPG/330px-Cuba_police_car_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cuba_police_car_01.JPG/440px-Cuba_police_car_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3019" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuba_police_car_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Lada_Riva" title="Lada Riva">Lada Riva</a> police car in <a href="/wiki/Holgu%C3%ADn" title="Holguín">Holguín</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All law enforcement agencies are maintained under Cuba's Ministry of the Interior which is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolutionary_Armed_Forces" title="Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces">Revolutionary Armed Forces</a>. In Cuba, citizens can receive police assistance by dialing "106" on their <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">telephones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> The police force, which is referred to as "Policía Nacional Revolucionaria" or PNR is then expected to provide help. The Cuban government also has an agency called the <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_Directorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Intelligence Directorate">Intelligence Directorate</a> that conducts intelligence operations and maintains close ties with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service_(Russia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Security Service (Russia)">Russian Federal Security Service</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolutionary_Armed_Forces" title="Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces">Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cuba&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Cuba spent about <span class="nowrap">US$91.8 million</span> on its armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> In 1985, Cuba devoted more than 10% of its <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> to military expenditures.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> In response to perceived American aggression, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</a>, Cuba built up one of the largest armed forces in Latin America, second only to that of <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Armed_Forces" title="Brazilian Armed Forces">Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-military_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-military-179">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1975 until the late 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet military</a> assistance enabled Cuba to upgrade its military capabilities. After the loss of Soviet subsidies, Cuba scaled down the numbers of military personnel, from 235,000 in 1994 to about 60,000 in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cuba" title="Economy of Cuba">Economy of Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rationing_in_Cuba" title="Rationing in Cuba">Rationing in Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociolismo" title="Sociolismo">Sociolismo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">United States embargo against Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="862" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cuba.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cuban export composition, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cuban state claims to adhere to <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> principles in organizing its largely state-controlled <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a>. Most of the means of production are owned and run by the government and most of the labor force is employed by the state. Recent years have seen a trend toward more private sector employment. By 2006, public sector employment was 78% and private sector 22%, compared to 91.8% to 8.2% in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> Cuba's government spending as a percentage of GDP is 78.1 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Any firm wishing to hire a Cuban must pay the Cuban government, which in turn will pay the employee in Cuban pesos.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> The average monthly wage as of July 2013 is 466 <a href="/wiki/Cuban_pesos" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban pesos">Cuban pesos</a>, which are worth about US$19.<sup id="cite_ref-moneytalk_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moneytalk-184">[183]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Libreta_line_Havana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Libreta_line_Havana.jpg/220px-Libreta_line_Havana.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Libreta_line_Havana.jpg/330px-Libreta_line_Havana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Libreta_line_Havana.jpg/440px-Libreta_line_Havana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Libreta_line_Havana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People waiting in line at a libreta store in Havana</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuba has a dual currency system, whereby most wages and prices are set in Cuban pesos (CUP), while the tourist economy operates with <a href="/wiki/Convertible_peso" class="mw-redirect" title="Convertible peso">Convertible pesos</a> (CUC), set at par with the <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">US dollar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-moneytalk_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moneytalk-184">[183]</a></sup> Every Cuban household has a ration book (known as <a href="/wiki/Libreta" class="mw-redirect" title="Libreta">libreta</a>) entitling it to a monthly supply of food and other staples, which are provided at nominal cost.<sup id="cite_ref-dealsoff_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dealsoff-185">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before Fidel Castro's 1959 revolution, Cuba was one of the most advanced and successful countries in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-pbs.org_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs.org-186">[185]</a></sup> Cuba's capital, Havana, was a "glittering and dynamic city".<sup id="cite_ref-pbs.org_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs.org-186">[185]</a></sup> The country's economy in the early part of the century, fuelled by the sale of sugar to the United States, had grown wealthy. Cuba ranked 5th in the hemisphere in per capita income, 3rd in life expectancy, 2nd in per capita ownership of automobiles and telephones, and 1st in the number of television sets per inhabitant. Cuba's literacy rate, 76%, was the fourth highest in Latin America. Cuba also ranked 11th in the world in the number of doctors per capita. Several private clinics and hospitals provided services for the poor. Cuba's income distribution compared favorably with that of other Latin American societies. However, income inequality was a profound issue between city and countryside, especially between whites and blacks. Cubans lived in abysmal poverty in the countryside. A thriving middle class, according to PBS, held the promise of prosperity and social mobility.<sup id="cite_ref-pbs.org_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs.org-186">[185]</a></sup> According to Cuba historian Louis Perez of the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, "Havana was then what Las Vegas has become."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantiagoPeople_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/SantiagoPeople_01.JPG/220px-SantiagoPeople_01.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/SantiagoPeople_01.JPG/330px-SantiagoPeople_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/SantiagoPeople_01.JPG/440px-SantiagoPeople_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SantiagoPeople_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cigar production in <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Cuban revolution and before the collapse of the Soviet Union, Cuba depended on Moscow for substantial aid and sheltered markets for its exports. The removal of these subsidies sent the Cuban economy into a rapid depression known in Cuba as the <a href="/wiki/Special_Period" title="Special Period">Special Period</a>. Cuba took limited free market-oriented measures to alleviate severe shortages of food, consumer goods, and services. These steps included allowing some self-employment in certain retail and light manufacturing sectors, the legalization of the use of the <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">US dollar</a> in business, and the encouragement of <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cuba" title="Tourism in Cuba">tourism</a>. Cuba has developed a unique urban farm system (the <i><a href="/wiki/Organop%C3%B3nicos" title="Organopónicos">organopónicos</a></i>) to compensate for the end of food imports from the Soviet Union. It's widely viewed that the <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">U.S. embargo</a> which initiated as a result of discontent with nationalization of U.S.-citizen-held property and later perceived human rights violations hurt the Cuban economy. In 2009, the Cuban Government estimated they lost $685 million annually from the US embargo.<sup id="cite_ref-dollarsandsense.org_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dollarsandsense.org-188">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>The leadership of Cuba has called for reforms in the country's <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Cuba" title="Agriculture in Cuba">agricultural system</a>. In 2008, Raúl Castro began enacting agrarian reforms to boost food production, as at that time 80% of food was imported. The reforms enacted are aimed at expanding land usage and increasing efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-food_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-food-189">[188]</a></sup> Venezuela supplies Cuba with an estimated 110,000 barrels (17,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) a day of oil in exchange for money and the services of some 44,000 Cubans, most of them medical personnel, in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> Estimates place Venezuelan assistance at over 20% of the Cuban GDP for 2008–2010, similar to the aid flows from the Soviet Union in 1985–1988.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg/220px-Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg/330px-Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg/440px-Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4192" data-file-height="2797" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Havana_-_Cuba_-_2756.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cubans are now permitted to own small businesses in certain sectors.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, Cuba had exports of <span class="nowrap">US$2.4 billion</span>, ranking 114 of 226 world countries, and imports of <span class="nowrap">US$6.9 billion</span>, ranking 87 of 226 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> Its major export partners are Canada 17.7%, China 16.9%, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> 12.5%, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> 9%, and Spain 5.9% (2012).<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-193">[192]</a></sup> Cuba's major exports are sugar, nickel, tobacco, fish, medical products, citrus fruits, and coffee;<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-193">[192]</a></sup> imports include food, fuel, clothing, and machinery. Cuba presently holds debt in an amount estimated to be <span class="nowrap">$13 billion</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> approximately 38% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Heritage Foundation">Heritage Foundation</a>, Cuba is dependent on credit accounts that rotate from country to country.<sup id="cite_ref-catholic_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catholic-196">[195]</a></sup> Cuba's prior 35% supply of the world's export market for sugar has declined to 10% due to a variety of factors, including a global sugar commodity price drop that made Cuba less competitive on world markets.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> It was announced in 2008 that wage caps would be abandoned to improve the nation's productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cuba&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Cubans were allowed to build their own houses. According to Raúl Castro, they will be able to improve their houses with this new permission, but the government will not endorse these new houses or improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> There is virtually no homelessness in Cuba, and 85% of Cubans own their own homes and pay no property taxes or interest on their mortgages. Mortgage payments can’t exceed 10% of the combined household income.<sup id="cite_ref-dollarsandsense.org_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dollarsandsense.org-188">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 2, 2011, <i>The New York Times</i> reported Cuba as reaffirming their intent to legalize "buying and selling" of private property before the year's end. According to experts, the private sale of property could "transform Cuba more than any of the economic reforms announced by President Raúl Castro's government".<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> It will cut more than one million state jobs, including party bureaucrats who resist the changes.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> The new economic reforms effectively created a new economic system, referred by some as the "New Cuban Economy".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> In October 2013, Raúl said he intends to merge the two currencies. As of August 2016, the dual currency system remains in force.</p>
<p>In August 2012, a specialist of the "Cubaenergia Company" announced the opening of Cuba's first Solar Power Plant. As a member of the Cubasolar Group, there was also a mention of 10 additional plants in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resources">Resources</span></h3>
<p>Cuba's natural resources include sugar, tobacco, fish, citrus fruits, <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Cuba" title="Coffee production in Cuba">coffee</a>, beans, rice, potatoes, and livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> The output of Cuba's nickel mines that year was 71,000 tons, approaching 4% of world production.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-207">[206]</a></sup> As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cuba&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> its reserves were estimated at 5.5 million tons, over 7% of the world total.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-207">[206]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sherritt_International" title="Sherritt International">Sherritt International</a> of Canada operates a large nickel mining facility in <a href="/wiki/Moa,_Cuba" title="Moa, Cuba">Moa</a>. Cuba is also a major producer of refined <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, a by-product of nickel mining operations.<sup id="cite_ref-torres_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torres-208">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Oil exploration in 2005 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">US Geological Survey</a> revealed that the North Cuba Basin could produce about 4.6 billion barrels (730,000,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) to 9.3 billion barrels (1.48<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil. In 2006, Cuba started to test-drill these locations for possible exploitation.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cuba" title="Tourism in Cuba">Tourism in Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Varaderos_beach_(5982433102).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg/220px-Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg/330px-Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg/440px-Varaderos_beach_%285982433102%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4891" data-file-height="3239" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Varaderos_beach_(5982433102).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Varadero" title="Varadero">Varadero</a> beach</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism was initially restricted to enclave resorts where tourists would be segregated from Cuban society, referred to as "enclave tourism" and "tourism apartheid".<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> Contacts between foreign visitors and ordinary Cubans were <i>de facto</i> illegal between 1992 and 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Corbett_2002_33_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corbett_2002_33-211">[210]</a></sup> The rapid growth of tourism during the Special Period had widespread social and economic repercussions in Cuba, and led to speculation about the emergence of a two-tier economy.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba has tripled its market share of Caribbean tourism in the last decade;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2013)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> as a result of significant investment in tourism infrastructure, this growth rate is predicted to continue.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> <span class="nowrap">1.9 million</span> tourists visited Cuba in 2003, predominantly from Canada and the European Union, generating revenue of <span class="nowrap">US$2.1 billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> Cuba recorded 2,688,000 international tourists in 2011, the third-highest figure in the Caribbean (behind the Dominican Republic and Puerto Rico).<sup id="cite_ref-unwto_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unwto-215">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> sector caters to thousands of European, Latin American, Canadian, and American consumers every year.</p>
<p>Allegations of widespread <a href="/wiki/Sex_tourism" title="Sex tourism">sex tourism</a> are downplayed by the Cuban Justice minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Justice_Minister_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Justice_Minister-216">[215]</a></sup> According to a Government of Canada travel advice website, "Cuba is actively working to prevent child sex tourism, and a number of tourists, including Canadians, have been convicted of offences related to the corruption of minors aged 16 and under. Prison sentences range from 7 to 25 years."<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cuba" title="Geography of Cuba">Geography of Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuba_rel94.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cuba_rel94.jpg/220px-Cuba_rel94.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cuba_rel94.jpg/330px-Cuba_rel94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cuba_rel94.jpg/440px-Cuba_rel94.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1415" data-file-height="977" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuba_rel94.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A general map of Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuba is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of islands located in the northern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> at the confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and the Atlantic Ocean. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">19°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_parallel_north" title="24th parallel north">24°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/74th_meridian_west" title="74th meridian west">74°</a> and <a href="/wiki/85th_meridian_west" title="85th meridian west">85°W</a>. The United States lies 150 kilometers (93 miles) across the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a> to the north and northwest (to the closest tip of <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>), and <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a> 21&#160;km (13&#160;mi) to the north. <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> lies 210 kilometers (130 miles) across the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Channel" title="Yucatán Channel">Yucatán Channel</a> to the west (to the closest tip of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Catoche" title="Cabo Catoche">Cabo Catoche</a> in the State of <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> is 77&#160;km (48&#160;mi) to the east, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> (140&#160;km/87&#160;mi) and the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> to the south. Cuba is the principal island, surrounded by four smaller groups of islands: the <a href="/wiki/Colorados_Archipelago" title="Colorados Archipelago">Colorados Archipelago</a> on the northwestern coast, the <a href="/wiki/Sabana-Camag%C3%BCey_Archipelago" title="Sabana-Camagüey Archipelago">Sabana-Camagüey Archipelago</a> on the north-central Atlantic coast, the <a href="/wiki/Jardines_de_la_Reina" title="Jardines de la Reina">Jardines de la Reina</a> on the south-central coast and the <a href="/wiki/Canarreos_Archipelago" title="Canarreos Archipelago">Canarreos Archipelago</a> on the southwestern coast.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg/220px-Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg" width="220" height="84" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg/330px-Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg/440px-Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6029" data-file-height="2300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Maestra_panorama1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sierra_Maestra" title="Sierra Maestra">Sierra Maestra</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main island, named Cuba, is 1,250&#160;km (780&#160;mi) long, constituting most of the nation's land area (104,556&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (40,369&#160;sq&#160;mi)) and is the largest island in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">17th-largest island</a> in the world by land area. The main island consists mostly of flat to rolling plains apart from the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Maestra" title="Sierra Maestra">Sierra Maestra</a> mountains in the southeast, whose highest point is <a href="/wiki/Pico_Turquino" title="Pico Turquino">Pico Turquino</a> (1,974&#160;m (6,476&#160;ft)).</p>
<p>The second-largest island is <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a> (Isle of Youth) in the Canarreos archipelago, with an area of 2,200&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (849&#160;sq&#160;mi). Cuba has an official area (land area) of 109,884&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (42,426&#160;sq&#160;mi). Its area is 110,860&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (42,803&#160;sq&#160;mi) including coastal and territorial waters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Cuba">Climate of Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valle_vinales_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Valle_vinales_1.jpg/220px-Valle_vinales_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Valle_vinales_1.jpg/330px-Valle_vinales_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Valle_vinales_1.jpg/440px-Valle_vinales_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valle_vinales_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1ales_Valley" title="Viñales Valley">Viñales Valley</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the entire island south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>, the local climate is tropical, moderated by northeasterly trade winds that blow year-round. The temperature is also shaped by the Caribbean current, which brings in warm water from the equator. This makes the climate of Cuba warmer than that of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, which is at around the same latitude as Cuba but has a subtropical rather than a tropical climate. In general (with local variations), there is a drier season from November to April, and a rainier season from May to October. The average temperature is 21&#160;°C (69.8&#160;°F) in January and 27&#160;°C (80.6&#160;°F) in July. The warm temperatures of the Caribbean Sea and the fact that Cuba sits across the entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> combine to make the country prone to frequent <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricanes</a>. These are most common in September and October.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<p>Cuba signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on June 12, 1992, and became a party to the convention on March 8, 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan" title="Biodiversity action plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, with one revision which was received by the convention on January 24, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>The revision comprises an action plan with time limits for each item, and an indication of the governmental body responsible for delivery. There is, however, virtually no information in that document about biodiversity itself. The country's fourth national report to the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">CBD</a>, however, contains a detailed breakdown of the numbers of species of each kingdom of life recorded from Cuba, the main groups being: <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> (17,801 species), <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> (270 species), <a href="/wiki/Chromista" title="Chromista">chromista</a> (707 species), <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a>-forming species (5844 species), <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> (9107 species) and <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoa</a> (1440 species).<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>As elsewhere in the world, vertebrate animals and flowering plants are well documented. The numbers recorded from Cuba for those groups are therefore likely to be close to the numbers which actually occur in Cuba. For most if not all of the other groups, however, the true numbers of species occurring in Cuba are likely to exceed, often considerably, the numbers of those recorded so far.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban people">Cuban people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cuba" title="Demographics of Cuba">Demographics of Cuba</a></div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Escuela_Lenin(estudiantes).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG/220px-Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG/330px-Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG/440px-Escuela_Lenin%28estudiantes%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Escuela_Lenin(estudiantes).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students of the Escuela Lenin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the official census of 2010, Cuba's population was 11,241,161, comprising 5,628,996 men and 5,612,165 women.<sup id="cite_ref-cubacensus2010_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cubacensus2010-221">[220]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> (9.88 births per thousand population in 2006)<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> is one of the lowest in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>. Although the country has grown by around 4 million people since 1961, the rate of increase had simultaneously began to fall during that period, and the population began to decline in 2006, with a fertility rate of 1.43 children per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>Indeed, this drop in fertility is among the largest in the Western Hemisphere,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> and is attributed largely to unrestricted access to legal abortion: Cuba's abortion rate was 58.6 per 1000 pregnancies in 1996, compared to an average of 35 in the Caribbean, 27 in Latin America overall, and 48 in Europe. Similarly, the use of <a href="/wiki/Contraception" class="mw-redirect" title="Contraception">contraceptives</a> is also widespread, estimated at 79% of the female population (in the upper third of countries in the Western Hemisphere).<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnoracial_groups">Ethnoracial groups</span></h3>
<p>Cuba's population is multiethnic, reflecting its complex colonial origins. Intermarriage between diverse groups is widespread, and consequently there is some discrepancy in reports of the country's racial composition: whereas the Institute for Cuban and Cuban-American Studies at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">University of Miami</a> determined that 62% of Cubans are black,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> the 2002 Cuban census found that a similar proportion of the population, 65.05%, was white.</p>
<p>In fact, the <a href="/wiki/Minority_Rights_Group_International" title="Minority Rights Group International">Minority Rights Group International</a> determined that "An objective assessment of the situation of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Cuban" title="Afro-Cuban">Afro-Cubans</a> remains problematic due to scant records and a paucity of systematic studies both pre- and post-revolution. Estimates of the percentage of people of African descent in the Cuban population vary enormously, ranging from 34% to 62%".<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>A study from 2014 found the <a href="/wiki/Autosome" title="Autosome">autosomal</a> genetic ancestry in Cuba to be 72% European, 20% African and 8% Native American;<sup id="cite_ref-plosgenetics.org_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plosgenetics.org-228">[227]</a></sup> 35% of maternal lineages derived from Cuban Native Americans, compared to 39% from Africa and 26% from Europe, but male lineages were European (82%) and African (18%), indicating the historical bias towards mating between foreign men and native women rather than the inverse.<sup id="cite_ref-plosgenetics.org_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plosgenetics.org-228">[227]</a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a> make up about 1% of the population, and are largely of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Cuban" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Cuban">Chinese ancestry</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Filipinos" title="Filipinos">Filipinos</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese</a><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many are descendants of farm laborers brought to the island by Spanish and American contractors during the 19th and early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> The currently recorded number of Cubans with Chinese ancestry is 114,240.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Afro-Cubans" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Cubans">Afro-Cubans</a> are descended primarily from the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba people</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Unreliable source removed: joshuaproject.net (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as well as several thousand <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North African</a> refugees, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawi Arabs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration_and_emigration">Immigration and emigration</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_immigration_to_Cuba" title="Spanish immigration to Cuba">Spanish immigration to Cuba</a></div>
<p>Immigration and emigration have played a prominent part in Cuba's demographic profile. Between the 18th and early 20th century, large waves of <a href="/wiki/Canarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Canarian people">Canarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusians" title="Andalusians">Andalusian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician people">Galician</a>, and other Spanish people immigrated to Cuba. Between 1899–1930 alone, close to a million Spaniards entered the country, though many would eventually return to Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup> Other prominent immigrant groups included French,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, as well as small number of descendants of U.S. citizens who arrived in Cuba in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.</p>
<p>Post-revolution Cuba has been characterized by significant levels of emigration, which has led to a <a href="/wiki/Cuban_exile" title="Cuban exile">large and influential diaspora community</a>. During the three decades after January 1959, more than one million Cubans of all social classes — constituting 10% of the total population — <a href="/wiki/Cuban_migration_to_Miami" title="Cuban migration to Miami">emigrated to the United States</a>, a proportion that matches the extent of emigration to the U.S. from the Caribbean as a whole during that period.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pedraza_2007_.3F_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedraza_2007_.3F-237">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Falk_1988_74_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falk_1988_74-238">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pedraza_2007_5_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedraza_2007_5-240">[239]</a></sup> Other common destinations include Spain, <a href="/wiki/Cubans_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubans in the United Kingdom">the United Kingdom</a>, Canada, <a href="/wiki/Cuban_immigration_to_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban immigration to Mexico">Mexico</a>, and Sweden, among others. Those who left the country typically did so by sea, in small boats and fragile rafts. On September 9, 1994, the U.S. and Cuban governments agreed that the U.S. would grant at least 20,000 visas annually in exchange for Cuba's pledge to prevent further unlawful departures on boats.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cuba" title="Religion in Cuba">Religion in Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG/220px-2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG/330px-2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG/440px-2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-Catedral_de_San_Cristobal_anagoria_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Havana_Cathedral" title="Havana Cathedral">Havana Cathedral</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, the religious affiliation of the country was estimated by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Forum" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Forum">Pew Forum</a> to be 65% Christian (60% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> or about 6.9 million in 2016, 5% <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> or about 575,000 in 2016), 23% unaffiliated, 17% <a href="/wiki/Folk_religion" title="Folk religion">folk religion</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">santería</a>), and the remaining 0.4% consisting of other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-pewrel_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewrel-242">[241]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba is officially a secular state. Religious freedom increased through the 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup> with the government amending the constitution in 1992 to drop the state's characterization as atheistic.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_2003_4_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_2003_4-244">[243]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> is the largest religion, with its origins in Spanish colonization. Despite less than half of the population identifying as Catholics in 2006, it nonetheless remains the dominant faith.<sup id="cite_ref-catholic_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catholic-196">[195]</a></sup> Pope John Paul II and Pope Benedict XVI visited Cuba in 1998 and 2011, respectively, and Pope Francis visited Cuba in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup> Prior to each papal visit, the Cuban government pardoned prisoners as a humanitarian gesture.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government's relaxation of restrictions on <a href="/wiki/House_church" title="House church">house churches</a> in the 1990s led to an explosion of <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a>, with some groups claiming as many as 100,000 members. However, <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestant">Evangelical Protestant</a> sects, organized into the umbrella Cuban Council of Churches, remain much more powerful.<sup id="cite_ref-Edmonds_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edmonds-249">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>The religious landscape of Cuba is also strongly defined by <a href="/wiki/Syncretisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncretisms">syncretisms</a> of various kinds. Christianity is often practiced in tandem with <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">Santería</a>, a mixture of Catholicism and mostly African faiths, which include a number of cults. La Virgen de la Caridad del Cobre (the Virgin of <i>Cobre</i>) is the Catholic patroness of Cuba, and a symbol of Cuban culture. In Santería, she has been syncretized with the goddess <a href="/wiki/Oshun" title="Oshun">Oshun</a>.</p>
<p>Cuba also hosts small communities of <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (500 in 2012), <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, and members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá'í">Bahá'í</a> Faith.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several well-known Cuban religious figures have operated outside the island, including the humanitarian and author <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Armando_P%C3%A9rez" title="Jorge Armando Pérez">Jorge Armando Pérez</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<p>The official language of Cuba is <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and the vast majority of Cubans speak it. Spanish as spoken in Cuba is known as <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Spanish" title="Cuban Spanish">Cuban Spanish</a> and is a form of <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Spanish" title="Caribbean Spanish">Caribbean Spanish</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lucum%C3%AD_language" title="Lucumí language">Lucumí</a>, a dialect of the West African language <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">Yoruba</a>, is also used as a <a href="/wiki/Liturgical_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Liturgical language">liturgical language</a> by practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">Santería</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup> and so only as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a> is the second largest language in Cuba, and is spoken by <a href="/wiki/Haitians" title="Haitians">Haitian</a> immigrants and their descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[252]</a></sup> Other languages spoken by immigrants include <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">Corsican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[253]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Cuba" title="Media of Cuba">Media of Cuba</a></div>
<p>The Cuban government and Communist Party of Cuba control almost all media in Cuba.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press">Press</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Cuba" title="List of newspapers in Cuba">List of newspapers in Cuba</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span></h3>
