<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">Internet</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Cuba" title="Internet in Cuba">Internet in Cuba</a> has some of the lowest penetration rates in the Western hemisphere, and all content is subject to review by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Revolutionary_Orientation" title="Department of Revolutionary Orientation">Department of Revolutionary Orientation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bedroses_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedroses-255">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ETECSA" title="ETECSA">ETECSA</a> operates 118 cybercafes in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-bedroses_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedroses-255">[254]</a></sup> The government of Cuba provides an online encyclopedia website called <a href="/wiki/EcuRed" title="EcuRed">EcuRed</a> that operates in a "<a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wiki</a>" format.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup> Internet access is limited.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup> The sale of computer equipment is strictly regulated. Internet access is controlled, and e-mail is closely monitored.<sup id="cite_ref-rsf_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsf-258">[257]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cuba" title="Culture of Cuba">Culture of Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Trova_Santiago_Cuba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A local musical house, Casa de la Trova in Santiago de Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuban culture is influenced by its melting pot of cultures, primarily those of Spain and Africa. After the 1959 revolution, the government started a national literacy campaign, offered free education to all and established rigorous sports, ballet and music programs.<sup id="cite_ref-hsas_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hsas-259">[258]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:208px;max-width:208px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg/100px-Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg" width="100" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg/150px-Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg/200px-Gloria_Estefan_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="333" data-file-height="465" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Celia_Cruz_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celia_Cruz_1.jpg/100px-Celia_Cruz_1.jpg" width="100" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celia_Cruz_1.jpg/150px-Celia_Cruz_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celia_Cruz_1.jpg/200px-Celia_Cruz_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">Gloria Estefan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celia_Cruz" title="Celia Cruz">Celia Cruz</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cuba" title="Music of Cuba">Music of Cuba</a></div>
<p>Cuban music is very rich and is the most commonly known expression of Cuban culture. The central form of this music is <a href="/wiki/Son_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Son (music)">Son</a>, which has been the basis of many other musical styles like "<a href="/wiki/Danz%C3%B3n" title="Danzón">Danzón</a> de nuevo ritmo", <a href="/wiki/Mambo_(music)" title="Mambo (music)">mambo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cha-cha-cha_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cha-cha-cha (music)">cha-cha-chá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa music</a>. Rumba ("de cajón o de solar") music originated in the early Afro-Cuban culture, mixed with Hispanic elements of style.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tres_(musical_instrument)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tres (musical instrument)">Tres</a> was invented in Cuba from Hispanic cordophone instruments models (the instrument is actually a fusion of elements from the Spanish guitar and lute). Other traditional Cuban instruments are of African origin, <a href="/wiki/Neo-Ta%C3%ADno_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Taíno nations">Taíno</a> origin, or both, such as the <a href="/wiki/Maraca" title="Maraca">maracas</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCiro" title="Güiro">güiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADmbula" title="Marímbula">marímbula</a> and various wooden drums including the <a href="/wiki/Mayohuac%C3%A1n" title="Mayohuacán">mayohuacán</a>.</p>
<p>Popular Cuban music of all styles has been enjoyed and praised widely across the world. Cuban classical music, which includes music with strong African and European influences, and features symphonic works as well as music for soloists, has received international acclaim thanks to composers like <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Lecuona" title="Ernesto Lecuona">Ernesto Lecuona</a>. Havana was the heart of the <a href="/wiki/Rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap">rap</a> scene in Cuba when it began in the 1990s.</p>
<p>During that time, <a href="/wiki/Reggaet%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Reggaetón">reggaetón</a> was growing in popularity. In 2011, the Cuban state denounced reggaeton as degenerate, directed reduced "low-profile" airplay of the genre (but did not ban it entirely) and banned the megahit <i>Chupi Chupi</i> by <a href="/wiki/Osmani_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Osmani García">Osmani García</a>, characterizing its description of sex as "the sort which a prostitute would carry out".<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[260]</a></sup> In December 2012, the Cuban government officially banned sexually explicit reggaeton songs and music videos from radio and television.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[262]</a></sup> As well as pop, classical and rock are very popular in Cuba.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_cuisine" title="Cuban cuisine">Cuban cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubanfood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cubanfood.jpg/220px-Cubanfood.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cubanfood.jpg/330px-Cubanfood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cubanfood.jpg/440px-Cubanfood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubanfood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A traditional meal of <i>ropa vieja</i> (shredded flank steak in a tomato sauce base), black beans, yellow rice, plantains and fried yuca with beer</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Havane_(1)_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg/220px-La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg/330px-La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg/440px-La_Havane_%281%29_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Havane_(1)_Tamales_pli%C3%A9s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cuban-style tamales</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuban cuisine is a fusion of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_cuisine" title="Caribbean cuisine">Caribbean cuisines</a>. Cuban recipes share spices and techniques with Spanish cooking, with some Caribbean influence in spice and flavor. Food rationing, which has been the norm in Cuba for the last four decades, restricts the common availability of these dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[263]</a></sup> The traditional Cuban meal is not served in courses; all food items are served at the same time.</p>
<p>The typical meal could consist of plantains, black beans and rice, <i><a href="/wiki/Ropa_vieja" title="Ropa vieja">ropa vieja</a></i> (shredded beef), <a href="/wiki/Cuban_bread" title="Cuban bread">Cuban bread</a>, pork with onions, and tropical fruits. Black beans and rice, referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Moros_y_cristianos" title="Moros y cristianos">moros y cristianos</a></i> (or <i>moros</i> for short), and plantains are staples of the Cuban diet. Many of the meat dishes are cooked slowly with light sauces. Garlic, cumin, oregano, and bay leaves are the dominant spices.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_literature" title="Cuban literature">Cuban literature</a></div>
<p>Cuban literature began to find its voice in the early 19th century. Dominant themes of independence and freedom were exemplified by José Martí, who led the Modernist movement in Cuban literature. Writers such as <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Nicolás Guillén">Nicolás Guillén</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Z._Tallet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="José Z. Tallet (page does not exist)">José Z. Tallet</a> focused on literature as social protest. The poetry and novels of <a href="/wiki/Dulce_Mar%C3%ADa_Loynaz" title="Dulce María Loynaz">Dulce María Loynaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lezama_Lima" title="José Lezama Lima">José Lezama Lima</a> have been influential. Romanticist <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Barnet" title="Miguel Barnet">Miguel Barnet</a>, who wrote <i>Everyone Dreamed of Cuba</i>, reflects a more melancholy Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alejo_Carpentier" title="Alejo Carpentier">Alejo Carpentier</a> was important in the <a href="/wiki/Magic_realism" title="Magic realism">Magic realism</a> movement. Writers such as <a href="/wiki/Reinaldo_Arenas" title="Reinaldo Arenas">Reinaldo Arenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Cabrera_Infante" title="Guillermo Cabrera Infante">Guillermo Cabrera Infante</a>, and more recently <a href="/wiki/Da%C3%ADna_Chaviano" title="Daína Chaviano">Daína Chaviano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Juan_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Pedro Juan Gutiérrez">Pedro Juan Gutiérrez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zo%C3%A9_Vald%C3%A9s" title="Zoé Valdés">Zoé Valdés</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Rosales" title="Guillermo Rosales">Guillermo Rosales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Padura" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonardo Padura">Leonardo Padura</a> have earned international recognition in the post-revolutionary era, though many of these writers have felt compelled to continue their work in exile due to ideological control of media by the Cuban authorities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span></h3>
<p>Dance holds a privileged position in Cuban culture. <a href="/wiki/Popular_dance" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular dance">Popular dance</a> is considered an essential part of life, and <a href="/wiki/Concert_dance" title="Concert dance">concert dance</a> is supported by the government and includes internationally renowned companies such as the <a href="/wiki/Ballet_Nacional_de_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballet Nacional de Cuba">Ballet Nacional de Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnn_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnn-266">[265]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Cuba" title="Sport in Cuba">Sport in Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023,_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023%2C_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023%2C_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023%2C_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023%2C_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023%2C_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1985-1004-023,_Teofilo_Stevenson_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cuban former boxer <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Stevenson" title="Teófilo Stevenson">Teófilo Stevenson</a>, widely considered to be one of the greatest boxers of all-time</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due to historical associations with the United States, many Cubans participate in sports which are popular in North America, rather than sports traditionally promoted in other Latin American nations. <a href="/wiki/Baseball_in_Cuba" title="Baseball in Cuba">Baseball</a> is by far the most popular; other sports and pastimes include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Track and field athletics">athletics</a>. Cuba is a dominant force in <a href="/wiki/Amateur_boxing" title="Amateur boxing">amateur boxing</a>, consistently achieving high medal tallies in major international competitions. Cuba also provides a <a href="/wiki/Cuba_at_the_Olympics" title="Cuba at the Olympics">national team</a> that competes in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[266]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Cuba" title="Education in Cuba">Education in Cuba</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg/220px-Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg/330px-Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg/440px-Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A0_de_La_Habana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_of_Havana" title="University of Havana">University of Havana</a>, founded in 1728</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Havana" title="University of Havana">University of Havana</a> was founded in 1728 and there are a number of other well-established <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Cuba" title="List of universities in Cuba">colleges and universities</a>. In 1957, just before Castro came to power, the literacy rate was fourth in the region at almost 80% according to the United Nations, higher than in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-asce_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asce-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup> Castro created an entirely state-operated system and banned private institutions. School attendance is compulsory from ages six to the end of basic secondary education (normally at age 15), and all students, regardless of age or gender, wear school uniforms with the color denoting grade level. Primary education lasts for six years, secondary education is divided into basic and pre-university education.<sup id="cite_ref-siteresources.worldbank.org_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siteresources.worldbank.org-269">[268]</a></sup> Cuba's <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of 99.8 percent<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-193">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mdgs.un.org_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mdgs.un.org-270">[269]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_literacy_rate" title="List of countries by literacy rate">tenth-highest globally</a>, due largely to the provision of free education at every level.<sup id="cite_ref-LiteracyC_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiteracyC-271">[270]</a></sup> Cuba's high school graduation rate is 94 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup></p>
<p>Higher education is provided by universities, higher institutes, higher <a href="/wiki/Pedagogical" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedagogical">pedagogical</a> institutes, and higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_institutions_using_the_term_%22institute_of_technology%22_or_%22polytechnic%22" title="List of institutions using the term &quot;institute of technology&quot; or &quot;polytechnic&quot;">polytechnic</a> institutes. The Cuban Ministry of Higher Education operates a scheme of distance education which provides regular afternoon and evening courses in rural areas for agricultural workers. Education has a strong political and ideological emphasis, and students progressing to higher education are expected to have a commitment to the goals of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-siteresources.worldbank.org_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siteresources.worldbank.org-269">[268]</a></sup> Cuba has provided state subsidized education to a limited number of foreign nationals at the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_School_of_Medicine_(Cuba)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American School of Medicine (Cuba)">Latin American School of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_la_Habana" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad de la Habana">Universidad de la Habana</a> (1680th worldwide), <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Superior_Polit%C3%A9cnico_Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Echeverr%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Superior Politécnico José Antonio Echeverría">Instituto Superior Politécnico José Antonio Echeverría</a> (2893rd) and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santiago_de_Cuba" title="University of Santiago de Cuba">University of Santiago de Cuba</a> (3831st).<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[274]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Cuba" title="Healthcare in Cuba">Healthcare in Cuba</a></div>
<p>Cuba's <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> at birth is 78 years.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_193-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-193">[192]</a></sup> Historically, Cuba has ranked high in numbers of medical personnel and has made significant contributions to world health since the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-asce_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asce-87">[86]</a></sup> Today, Cuba has <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> and although shortages of medical supplies persist, there is no shortage of medical personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-whiteford_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whiteford-276">[275]</a></sup> Primary care is available throughout the island and infant and maternal mortality rates compare favorably with those in developed nations.<sup id="cite_ref-whiteford_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whiteford-276">[275]</a></sup></p>
<p>Post-Revolution Cuba initially experienced an overall worsening in terms of disease and infant mortality rates in the 1960s when half its 6,000 doctors left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup> Recovery occurred by the 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-bethell_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bethell-77">[76]</a></sup> and the country's healthcare has been widely praised.<sup id="cite_ref-Feinsilver_1989_4to5_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feinsilver_1989_4to5-278">[277]</a></sup> The Communist government asserted that universal health care was to become a priority of state planning and progress was made in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup> Like the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cuba" title="Economy of Cuba">Cuban economy</a>, Cuban medical care suffered from severe material shortages following the end of Soviet subsidies in 1991, followed by a tightening of the U.S. embargo in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup></p>
<p>Challenges include low salaries for doctors,<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup> poor facilities, poor provision of equipment, and the frequent absence of essential drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup> Cuba has the highest doctor-to-population ratio in the world and has sent thousands of doctors to more than 40 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, Cuba is "known the world over for its ability to train excellent doctors and nurses who can then go out to help other countries in need". As of September 2014 there are around 50,000 Cuban-trained health care workers aiding 66 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup> Cuban physicians have played a leading role in combating the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the UN, the life expectancy in Cuba is 78.3 years (76.2 for males and 80.4 for females). This ranks Cuba 37th in the world and 3rd in the Americas, behind only Canada and Chile, and just ahead of the United States. Infant mortality in Cuba declined from 32 infant deaths per 1,000 live births in 1957, to 10 in 1990–95.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup> Infant mortality in 2000–2005 was 6.1 per 1,000 live births. Its <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> is 5.13.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_193-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-193">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mdgs.un.org_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mdgs.un.org-270">[269]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Cuba, there is a need to import certain <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_drug" title="Pharmaceutical drug">pharmaceutical drugs</a>. Therefore, the Quimefa Pharmaceutical Business Group (FARMACUBA) was developed under the Ministry of Basic Industry (MINBAS). This group also handles the exporting of pharmaceuticals, and provide technical information for the production of these drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup> Isolated from the West, Cuba developed the successful lung cancer vaccine, <a href="/wiki/CimaVax-EGF" title="CimaVax-EGF">Cimavax</a>, which now is available to US researchers for the first time, along with other novel Cuban cancer treatments. The vaccine has been available for free to the Cuban population since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[287]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a> CEO Candace Johnson: "They've had to do more with less, so they've had to be even more innovative with how they approach things. For over 40 years, they have had a preeminent immunology community."<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Cuba became the first country to eradicate <a href="/wiki/Mother-to-child_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother-to-child transmission">mother-to-child transmission</a> of HIV and syphilis,<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup> a milestone hailed by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> as "one of the greatest public health achievements possible".<sup id="cite_ref-Graun_eradication_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graun_eradication-291">[290]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-120">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2012/10/16/world/americas/cuba-travel-policy/">CNN: "Cuba eases travel restriction for citizens" by Ben Brumfield</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160304095615/http://www.cnn.com/2012/10/16/world/americas/cuba-travel-policy/">Archived</a> March 4, 2016, at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. October 16, 2012 |<i>Until now, Cubans had to pay $150 for an exit visa. A resident in the country that the Cuban wanted to visit would also have to write a letter of invitation. Fees associated with the letter ran as high as $200. That's a steep price in a country where the average official monthly income is about $20.</i></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-hrw1999-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-hrw1999_145-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-hrw1999_145-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.hrw.org/reports/1999/cuba/Cuba996-05.htm">"Cuba's Repressive Machinery – V. <li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/10517497">"Number of Cuban political prisoners dips – rights group"</a>. BBC News. July 5, 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 2,</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACuba&amp;rft.atitle=Number+of+Cuban+political+prisoners+dips+%93+rights+group&amp;rft.date=2010-07-05&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fnews%2F10517497&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_1996_159.2C161-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_1996_159.2C161_147-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses1996">Gleijeses 1996</a>, pp.&#160;159, 161: "Cuba's relationship with Algeria in 1961–5&#160;... clashes with the image of Cuban foreign policy—cynical ploys of a [Soviet] client state—that prevails not only in the United States but also in many European capitals.&#160;... The aid Cuba gave Algeria in 1961–2 had nothing to do with the East-West conflict. Its roots predate Castro's victory in 1959 and lie in the Cubans' widespread identification with the struggle of the Algerian people."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_2010_327-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_2010_327_148-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses2010">Gleijeses 2010</a>, p.&#160;327: "The dispatch of 36,000 Cuban soldiers to Angola between November 1975 and April 1976 stunned the world;&#160;... by 1988, there were 55,000 Cuban soldiers in Angola."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_2002_392-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_2002_392_149-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses2002">Gleijeses 2002</a>, p.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QHWGwG71hzMC&amp;pg=PA392">392</a>: "After Angola, Cuba's largest military intervention was in Ethiopia, where in 1978 16,000 Cuban troops helped repulse the invading Somali army."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Tareke_2009_62to63-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Tareke_2009_62to63_150-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFTareke2009">Tareke 2009</a>, pp.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dRIfYPTZxJsC&amp;pg=PA62">62–3</a>. Tareke refers here to the training given to 10&#160;members of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">Eritrean Liberation Front</a> in 1968 during the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean struggle for independence</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_1997_50-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_1997_50_151-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses1997">Gleijeses 1997</a>, p.&#160;50: "On 14–16 October 1960, [Guinean president Ahmed Sékou] Touré went to Havana. It was the first visit of an African chief of state to Cuba. The following year Cuba's foreign aid programme to Third World governments began when fifteen students from Guinea arrived in Havana to attend the university or technical institutes."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_1997_45-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_1997_45_152-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses1997">Gleijeses 1997</a>, p.&#160;45: "Joining the rebellion in 1966, and remaining through the war's end in 1974, this was the longest Cuban intervention in Africa before the despatch of troops to Angola in November 1975. It was also the most successful. As the Guinean paper <i>Nõ Pintcha</i> declared, 'The Cubans' solidarity was decisive for our struggle<span style="padding-right:.2em;">'</span>".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Gleijeses_2002_227-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gleijeses_2002_227_153-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGleijeses2002">Gleijeses 2002</a>, p.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QHWGwG71hzMC&amp;pg=PA227&amp;dq=%22not+very+important%22">227</a>. The Cuban contribution to the independence of Mozambique was not very important.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTERamazani1975.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D7ETnbmUmxoUC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D-154"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamazani1975.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D7ETnbmUmxoUC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D_154-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFRamazani1975">Ramazani 1975</a>, p.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=7ETnbmUmxoUC&amp;pg=PA91">91</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_6-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_1989_6_155-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFDom.C3.ADnguez1989">Domínguez 1989</a>, p.&#160;6: "Cuba is a small country, but it has the foreign policy of a big power."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Feinsilver_1989_2-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Feinsilver_1989_2_156-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFFeinsilver1989">Feinsilver 1989</a>, p.&#160;2: "Cuba has projected disproportionately greater power and influence through military might&#160;... through economic largesse&#160;... as a mediator in regional conflicts, and as a forceful and persuasive advocate of Third World interests in international forums. Cuba's scientific achievements, while limited, are also being shared with other Third World countries, thereby furthering Cuban influence and prestige abroad."</span></li>

Despite U.S. hostility toward Cuba, a U.S. government document stated in 1982 that the 'Cuban Revolution has managed social achievements, especially in education and health care, that are highly respected in the Third World&#160;... , [including] a national health care program that is superior in the Third World and rivals that of numerous developed countries.<span style="padding-right:.2em;">'</span>"</span></li>
